\item Claim: The user also made a clear versioning decision.\allowbreak{} \textbf{FACT:} The user wanted \textbf{major.minor.patch semantic versioning} for all components/\allowbreak{}packages and for the complete game package.\allowbreak{} The user explicitly did \textbf{not} want build numbers or build dates in filenames.\allowbreak{} Instead, those details should live in metadata.\allowbreak{} This became part of the future build/\allowbreak{}package design.\allowbreak{}

\subsubsection{PROMOTE-0035 - architecturedoccandidate}

\begin{itemize}
\item Source conversation: \texttt{Dominium\_\allowbreak{}Architecture\_\allowbreak{}II}

\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{PROMOTE-0038 - architecturedoccandidate}

\begin{itemize}
\item Source conversation: \texttt{Dominium\_\allowbreak{}Architecture\_\allowbreak{}III}
\item Proposed target: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}architecture/\allowbreak{}** after target selection}
\item Validation required: source check, authority-\allowbreak{}order check, link check, generated output validator, FAST
\item Recommended microtask: \texttt{DOC-\allowbreak{}PROMOTION-\allowbreak{}PROMOTE-\allowbreak{}0038}
\item Claim: This context matters because the rest of the conversation happened inside those constraints.\allowbreak{} The launcher could not become a dumping ground for OS-\allowbreak{}specific behavior, sim mutation, renderer decisions, or nondeterministic game-\allowbreak{}state changes.\allowbreak{} It had to fit the project's deterministic layering.\allowbreak{}
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{PROMOTE-0050 - architecturedoccandidate}

\begin{itemize}
\item Source conversation: \texttt{dominium\_\allowbreak{}full\_\allowbreak{}conversation}
\item Proposed target: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}architecture/\allowbreak{}** after target selection}
\item Validation required: source check, authority-\allowbreak{}order check, link check, generated output validator, FAST
\item Recommended microtask: \texttt{DOC-\allowbreak{}PROMOTION-\allowbreak{}PROMOTE-\allowbreak{}0050}
\item Claim: The user then redirected the entire plan.\allowbreak{} They argued that native OS widget GUI tools already exist through Visual Studio, Xcode, etc.\allowbreak{} The project needed a cross-\allowbreak{}platform rendered tool environment that uses the same CLI, TUI, and rendered GUI systems as the client.\allowbreak{} The old UI Editor and Tool Editor were good exploratory ideas but bad final products.\allowbreak{} This produced the Dominium Workbench concept.\allowbreak{}
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{PROMOTE-0054 - planningdoccandidate}

\begin{itemize}
\item Source conversation: \texttt{dominium\_\allowbreak{}setup}
\item Proposed target: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}planning/\allowbreak{}** after target selection}
\item Validation required: source check, authority-\allowbreak{}order check, link check, generated output validator, FAST
\item Recommended microtask: \texttt{DOC-\allowbreak{}PROMOTION-\allowbreak{}PROMOTE-\allowbreak{}0054}
\item Claim: The user later asked where to create Visual Studio and Xcode apps after opening the repo as a folder.\allowbreak{} The assistant advised that Visual Studio and Xcode projects should be generated through CMake, not hand-\allowbreak{}authored or treated as authoritative source files.\allowbreak{} This decision became consistent with later Codex prompts.\allowbreak{}
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{PROMOTE-0063 - architecturedoccandidate}

\begin{itemize}
\item Source conversation: \texttt{engine\_\allowbreak{}baseline\_\allowbreak{}architecture}
\item Proposed target: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}architecture/\allowbreak{}** after target selection}
\item Validation required: source check, authority-\allowbreak{}order check, link check, generated output validator, FAST
\item Recommended microtask: \texttt{DOC-\allowbreak{}PROMOTION-\allowbreak{}PROMOTE-\allowbreak{}0063}
\item Claim: The central architecture distinction was that Domino should be a reusable deterministic simulation substrate, while Dominium should be one game/\allowbreak{}product layer built on it.\allowbreak{} This came up immediately when the user asked for a total description of the project.\allowbreak{} It mattered because the user wants the code to be reusable for future games and possibly other engine projects.\allowbreak{}
\end{itemize}

\end{itemize}

Top things to know: 1.\allowbreak{} Workbench is not authority; it is a projection over contracts/\allowbreak{}services/\allowbreak{}commands/\allowbreak{}documents/\allowbreak{}evidence.\allowbreak{} 2.\allowbreak{} CLI, TUI, rendered GUI, native GUI, and headless should share one semantic spine.\allowbreak{} 3.\allowbreak{} TUI is first-\allowbreak{}class.\allowbreak{} 4.\allowbreak{} Rendered GUI is built on software renderer first; hardware later.\allowbreak{} 5.\allowbreak{} Native SDK GUIs remain optional projections.\allowbreak{} 6.\allowbreak{} UI is data-\allowbreak{}described through views, layouts, controls, widgets, themes, style tokens, and projections.\allowbreak{} 7.\allowbreak{} Visual edits should produce document patches and evidence.\allowbreak{} 8.\allowbreak{} Components, services, providers, packs, modules, workspaces, apps, and artifacts are distinct.\allowbreak{} 9.\allowbreak{} Workbench

\begin{enumerate}
\item C17 + C++17 is the mainline direction.\allowbreak{} 2.\allowbreak{} C89/\allowbreak{}C++98 is superseded for mainline, preserved only for retro/\allowbreak{}projection/\allowbreak{}archive thinking.\allowbreak{} 3.\allowbreak{} Pure C99 was rejected as too weak for Dominium-\allowbreak{}scale modularity.\allowbreak{} 4.\allowbreak{} Pure C++11 was rejected as unnecessarily conservative.\allowbreak{} 5.\allowbreak{} C17 owns stable law and ABI-\allowbreak{}adjacent substrate.\allowbreak{} 6.\allowbreak{} C++17 owns machinery, providers, apps, Workbench, and tools.\allowbreak{} 7.\allowbreak{} Public boundaries remain C-\allowbreak{}compatible, POD-\allowbreak{}only, versioned, and no-\allowbreak{}exception.\allowbreak{} 8.\allowbreak{} No STL/\allowbreak{}classes/\allowbreak{}templates/\allowbreak{}RTTI/\allowbreak{}exceptions cross stable ABI.\allowbreak{} 9.\allowbreak{} Full source-\allowbreak{}native builds should be 64-\allowbreak{}bit: x86\_\allowbreak{}64/\allowbreak{}arm64.\allowbreak{} 10.\allowbreak{} 32-\allowbreak{}bit is constrained/\allowbreak{}projection/\allowbreak{}archive only.\allowbreak{} 11.\allowbreak{} Little-\allowbreak{}endian mainline is accepted.\allowbreak{} 12.\allowbreak{} Save/\allowbreak{}replay/\allowbreak{}n
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Reader Brief Dominium Xstack Release Identity And Versioning}

\vonecallout{DomSlate}{Source}{\texttt{advisory} \texttt{human\_\allowbreak{}full\_\allowbreak{}text} \texttt{conversation\_\allowbreak{}advisory} Source: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}archive/\allowbreak{}conversations/\allowbreak{}Release\_\allowbreak{}Identity\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}Versioning/\allowbreak{}Dominium\_\allowbreak{}XStack\_\allowbreak{}Release\_\allowbreak{}Identity\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}Versioning\_\allowbreak{}\_\allowbreak{}06\_\allowbreak{}reader\_\allowbreak{}brief.\allowbreak{}md}.\allowbreak{} Reason: reader-\allowbreak{}oriented conversation artifact.\allowbreak{}}

Summary: This chat designed a release identity/\allowbreak{}versioning architecture for Dominium/\allowbreak{}XStack.\allowbreak{} It moved from general versioning theory to a concrete layered model that separates strict SemVer components, SemVer-\allowbreak{}shaped product/\allowbreak{}suite release IDs, GBN/\allowbreak{}BII build provenance, channels/\allowbreak{}lifecycle, artifact names, platform targets, manifests, and capability-\allowbreak{}based compatibility.\allowbreak{}


\begin{enumerate}
\item Do not solve release identity with one number.\allowbreak{} 2.\allowbreak{} Strict SemVer is only for declared public APIs/\allowbreak{}contracts.\allowbreak{} 3.\allowbreak{} Products and suites may use SemVer-\allowbreak{}shaped IDs without strict SemVer semantics.\allowbreak{} 4.\allowbreak{} Products and suites are separate entity classes.\allowbreak{} 5.\allowbreak{} GBN is build provenance, not SemVer precedence.\allowbreak{} 6.\allowbreak{} BII should be structured manifest metadata.\allowbreak{} 7.\allowbreak{} Git SHA can identify local builds.\allowbreak{} 8.\allowbreak{} \texttt{stable} should not be encoded as \texttt{-\allowbreak{}stable}.\allowbreak{} 9.\allowbreak{} Hotfixes should normally be patch releases plus metadata.\allowbreak{} 10.\allowbreak{} dev/\allowbreak{}alpha/\allowbreak{}beta/\allowbreak{}rc are prerelease labels.\allowbreak{} 11.\allowbreak{}
\end{enumerate}

This chat decided that Dominium/\allowbreak{}XStack should use a layered identity architecture: strict SemVer for public API components, SemVer-\allowbreak{}shaped release IDs for products/\allowbreak{}suites, GBN/\allowbreak{}BII/\allowbreak{}hash for exact provenance, manifests for canonical truth, and capabilities/\allowbreak{}contracts for internal compatibility.\allowbreak{} The exact suite semantics, BII schema, target taxonomy, manifest schema, and capability registry still need formal work.\allowbreak{}

The user wanted to know whether they would stop working completely, whether critical functions would fail, wheth



\subsection{Reader Brief Dominium Timekeeping And 2038 Resilience}

\vonecallout{DomSlate}{Source}{\texttt{advisory} \texttt{human\_\allowbreak{}full\_\allowbreak{}text} \texttt{conversation\_\allowbreak{}advisory} Source: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}archive/\allowbreak{}conversations/\allowbreak{}Timekeeping\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}2038\_\allowbreak{}Resilience/\allowbreak{}Dominium\_\allowbreak{}Timekeeping\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}2038\_\allowbreak{}Resilience\_\allowbreak{}\_\allowbreak{}06\_\allowbreak{}reader\_\allowbreak{}brief.\allowbreak{}md}.\allowbreak{} Reason: reader-\allowbreak{}oriented conversation artifact.\allowbreak{}}

Summary: This chat developed a durable timekeeping framework, starting from Y2038 and ending with Dominium-\allowbreak{}specific architecture guidance.\allowbreak{} The key result is that Dominium should preserve a strict split: ACT for authoritative logical simulation, DSYS monotonic time for runtime/\allowbreak{}pacing, observer clocks for derived perception/\allowbreak{}replay, and civil/\allowbreak{}astronomical time as projection only.\allowbreak{}


\begin{enumerate}
\item Y2038 is about signed 32-\allowbreak{}bit time representations, not all 32-\allowbreak{}bit machines.\allowbreak{} 2.\allowbreak{} Some 32-\allowbreak{}bit apps will continue; vulnerable time functions may fail.\allowbreak{} 3.\allowbreak{} Clock rollback is not a general solution.\allowbreak{} 4.\allowbreak{} Unsigned 32-\allowbreak{}bit is not a future-\allowbreak{}proof absolute timestamp fix.\allowbreak{} 5.\allowbreak{} Signed 64-\allowbreak{}bit is the right baseline for long-\allowbreak{}lived project time.\allowbreak{} 6.\allowbreak{} One signed 64-\allowbreak{}bit nanosecond scalar is too narrow for ?10,000 years.\allowbreak{} 7.\allowbreak{} 100 ns and 1 ?s scalar ticks are practical for that range.\allowbreak{} 8.\allowbreak{} Split \texttt{int64 seconds + int32 nanos} is cleaner when possible.\allowbreak{} 9
\end{enumerate}


\subsection{In Chat Reader Dominium Timekeeping And 2038 Resilience}

\vonecallout{DomSlate}{Source}{\texttt{advisory} \texttt{human\_\allowbreak{}full\_\allowbreak{}text} \texttt{conversation\_\allowbreak{}advisory} Source: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}archive/\allowbreak{}conversations/\allowbreak{}Timekeeping\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}2038\_\allowbreak{}Resilience/\allowbreak{}Dominium\_\allowbreak{}Timekeeping\_\allowbreak{}and\_\allowbreak{}2038\_\allowbreak{}Resilience\_\allowbreak{}\_\allowbreak{}09\_\allowbreak{}in\_\allowbreak{}chat\_\allowbreak{}reader.\allowbreak{}md}.\allowbreak{} Reason: reader-\allowbreak{}oriented conversation artifact.\allowbreak{}}

Summary: This package preserves a chat about Y2038-\allowbreak{}safe timekeeping, durable timestamp representations, cross-\allowbreak{}platform temporal architecture, and Dominium's ACT/\allowbreak{}DSYS/\allowbreak{}observer time model.\allowbreak{}


The chat found that Dominium's core time model is already mostly correct.\allowbreak{} The project should keep ACT as logical authority, DSYS time as runtime/\allowbreak{}pacing only, observer clocks as derived perception/\allowbreak{}replay, and civil/\allowbreak{}astronomical time as a projection layer.\allowbreak{} The key future work is auditing edges: backend timers, serialization, wall-\allowbreak{}clock leakage, and current external platform facts.\allowbreak{}

\subsection{Reader Brief Dominium World Architecture}

\vonecallout{DomSlate}{Source}{\texttt{advisory} \texttt{human\_\allowbreak{}full\_\allowbreak{}text} \texttt{conversation\_\allowbreak{}advisory} Source: \texttt{docs/\allowbreak{}archive/\allowbreak{}conversations/\allowbreak{}World\_\allowbreak{}Architecture/\allowbreak{}Dominium\_\allowbreak{}World\_\allowbreak{}Architecture\_\allowbreak{}\_\allowbreak{}05\_\allowbreak{}reader\_\allowbreak{}brief.\allowbreak{}md}.\allowbreak{} Reason: reader-\allowbreak{}oriented conversation artifact.\allowbreak{}}
